Prologue

Evelyn was the first to break away from the clutch of her beast. So it was her that had and still has the best self-control out of all of us. It went like this, first, it was Evelyn, and then it was Taylor, Casiar, Avery, Cailin, Rebecka, Riordan, Allia, Elijah, and then me, Tristan. I was the last to break away from the claws of my beast. Today, I still have the hardest time, keeping my inner beast leashed. Every second, of every minute, of every hour, of every day, it was a battle, a constant battle I sometime wonder, if I would lose it completely. Yes, my siblings and I set all the rules all vampire must follow, but I knew, one day, I was going to break one of those rules we've laid down. For all it's worth, I pray to whoever is watching from above, that I wouldn't go down that road. I never wanted to go down that path again. Every time I close my eyes, my mind wanders back to that fateful long nights where I fought for control, and losing. It was Evelyn; Evelyn was my strength and still is today. You see, our blood was like a directional compass. When I found her, so many centuries ago, I knew that I wanted no harm to come to her, so I took her with me, though she fought me like the starving rogues we were then. She calmed a bit when I told her who I was, and she wanted to find the rest of our blood siblings. So that's what we did, Evelyn, Elijah, Riordan, Allia, and I. We traveled all over Scandinavia, rounding them up, explaining who we were. It wasn't hard. To my surprise, they were looking for us as well. Together, we pillage villages, draining them completely of blood. This went on for centuries, and today, I wondered if things would have been different, if Ulrika and Soren had guide us, taught us, cared for us, loved us. Would it have made a difference? After five thousand years, I still wondered, knowing very well, that I wouldn't find the answer. For centuries, I also kept up with my human life, the life that was taken away from me four thousand nine hundred and eighty years ago. From a distance, I watched them grow up, graduate, date, married, have children, and die, whether it was from sickness, or natural death. And every time, it hurt, knowing I would live forever, while they, one by one, die on me. Though I wanted so badly to cure them of every ailment, I held myself back. I never showed myself to them, not even today. What would they think? What would they say? In their minds, vampires didn't exist. Vampires were only in books and movies. Vampires were a figment of your imagination, after all. And though they don't know I exist, from the shadows, I watched them, I protect them, and I kill for them. And yes, you're probably thinking I should let go of my human life, but I can't, no matter how hard I tried. And for the record, I protect what is mine, be it vampire or human. Touch them, and you die. It is as simple as, you fuck with them, and you'll have to deal with me. Don't like it? Then don't fuck around, with what is mine.

Chapter One

BRIDGET

"Vendostrum!"
"What?" I shouted.
"I want you down here now!"
"I'm coming!" I shouted again and grabbed hold of the zip line. I pushed off the roof I was on and hoped the line wouldn't break as I zipped through empty air. I let go of the breath I was holding as I made it safely to the other roof. I let go of the line and crossed the roof to the fire escape and clattered noisily down it. I stomped over to Vincent and glared at him. "What is it now?"
"You're fired," Vincent said dryly.
"Excuse me?"
"Okay, you're not, but I want you on security."
"Oh," I said. "And here I was hoping to have a reason to strangle you."
"Bridget? Violent?"
I smirked. "You have no idea."
"Can you take security?"
"Of course," I said and turned. "And next time, call me Bridget. Nobody ever calls me by my last name."
He snorted. "Well, they should start. That's an awesome sounding last name."
"I'll get on that, Peterson."
"Get out, Vendostrum. Get your pretty ass in gear."
"I have to start now?"
"What? You expect to start next week?" he asked as I walked away from him.
"I expected to start tomorrow night!" I yelled at him.
"Nope, not happening, blondie!"
"I'm blondie, now? Make up your mind, Peterson!"
"Vendostrum it is!"
"Fuck you!" I shot back at him before getting into my car. I started it up and yawned. Pulling out, I turned and drove down Irving Avenue.
Fifteen minutes later, I pulled up my driveway and parked. I got out and walked the short distance to my front door. I quickly open it and entered, slamming the door shut and locking it. I dropped my keys on the small table by the door and headed for the bedroom, wondering if I'd get any sleep at all this week. I glanced at the alarm clock on my nightstand and groaned, seven in the fucking evening. I was going to drop dead before the night was through. Sighing, I yanked open my closet and pulled my uniform out, a black-on-black ensemble and quickly dressed. Pulling open the bottom drawer of my nightstand, I took out my sidearm and putting on my weapon belt, I holstered it. I grabbed up my earpiece and stepped from my room, heading for the front door. Earpiece in place, and a tiny microphone clipped on the collar of my shirt; I pressed a button and did a callout. "Bridget, calling in," I said as I got back into my car.
"Got it," Doris said into my earpiece.
"Where am I supposed to meet you?"
"A club called The Night Life."
"On Hopkins Lane?" I asked and pulled out of my driveway.
"Yep."
"What are we exactly doing? Just uh? guard the doors or something?" I asked five minutes later.
"Extraction of a suspect."
I almost swerved off the road. "Vincent said security, not going in and taking down a suspect black-ops style."
"Well, that fucker lied."
"We're just not going to storm in there, are we? I heard creatures of the night frequent that club."
Doris snorted. "What creatures of the night? Demons? Werewolves?"
I shrugged, though she couldn't see it. "Ever since I moved to Cali with my family sixteen years ago from Maryland, I've been hearing things."
"Such as?"
"Such as this state is vampire central."
"Do you believe it?"
I pulled to a stop in the parking lot and again shrugged. "I'm the type of person who believes what she sees. And I bet you fifty dollars that you'll be the first to freak out if the rumors are true."
"You are so on," Doris said, as I opened my door.
"Tell me where you are at, I'm here."
"I'm at the back entrance of the bar section of the club." I stepped from my car and slammed the door shut. I looked around and saw no one out and about, though there were a lot of cars besides mine. "Hurry your ass up," she said thirty seconds later. I blew out a breath and went around the club. This place gives me the creeps, I silently muttered, spotting my partner, Doris Callahan up ahead. "Officer Vendostrum," she called to me. "You took your time." I gave her my best icy glare as I walked up to her.
"Officer Callahan," I said politely. "Sorry for my late? arrival."
She leaned into me, and I bent so she could whisper in my ear. "You're such a rookie."
"Do we really have to be on formal terms?" I whispered back to her.
She straightened. "Nah, our boss is gone."
"Awesome, shorty," I said and straightened.
She glared up at me. "If you call me that one more time, I'm going to pistol whip you." Doris was five-foot-three compare to my height of six-foot-five stature, and we sometimes pick on each other about it. I smirked and nodded to the door.
"Are we going in?" She nodded. "I thought we're going in the club way?" Doris shrugged. "Fine, lead the way."
Doris turned and pulled open the door and entered with me following behind her. Slipping my hand into my pocket, I pulled out my badge, and holy fucking pus bucket, my skin crawled. Yep, I hate this place, I silently grumbled. The bartender came out from behind the bar and headed straight for us. "Don't tell me you forgot your badge again, Doris mouthed. I shook my head and flashed it at her.
"Can I help you wonderful officers with something?" the bartender asked, stopping in front of us.
We both flashed our badges at him. "We're here to apprehend a suspect," Doris said in her professional tone. "Your name is?"
"Cane, I'm the bartender here." She nodded as my eyes scanned the bar. This bar was too quiet, and it was giving me the heebie-jeebies. For one, a very pale, extremely pale guy was staring at me, unblinking. The redhead, sitting beside him was frowning at him and glancing at me. "Do you have a picture of the suspect? Maybe, I've seen him around."
"No need," I said, my eyes on the door, as it opened.
"Freeze!" Doris and I shouted in unison. He didn't, he pulled out a gun and fired. I knocked Doris to the floor, pulling out my own gun. I aimed it at the brown-haired, brown-eyed suspect and shot him in the gut. He screamed and dropped his gun to the floor. I rushed him, tackling him.
"Jose Hernandez?" I asked and cuffed him.
"You bitch!" he screamed at me in accented English.
"That would be me," I said and got off of him.
"You Nordic cunt!"
"Ow," I said dryly. "It's so nice that you recognize me." I kicked him over onto his back and got a good look at his wound. "Where are your three friends?" I asked as Cane and Doris came over to us. Doris bent and pressed a towel to his stomach. Huh, I must've been so focused on the suspect not to hear the conversation Doris had with him. Must work on that, I thought.
"I'm not telling you shit," he wheezed. I tuned into Doris and Cane and frowned.
"Why can't I call for the ambulance?" Doris asked the bartender.
"Because they're vampires, chickas," Jose gasped and smirked.
"And uh, you came here, because?" I asked. "And, who is they?"
"I came here to kill them."
I raised an eyebrow at him. "What did they ever do to you?" I asked, interested.
"Nothing."
"You are going to kill them, because they did nothing?"
"They're going to drink you dry without even thinking, and don't act like you believe me."
I shrugged. "It's called open-minded, sweetness." His eyes glinted, and I scowled at him.
"He's fading," Doris said to me. "Vincent is on his way. He can drive him to the hospital." I looked up at Cane and held back a shiver as I got a good look at his black eyes, and it didn't look like he was wearing contacts. Damn, I muttered. A hand landed on my shoulder, and I reacted instinctively. It was the redhead. Her hand flashed and clamped down on my arm, preventing me from drawing my gun.
"Easy there officer," she said, smiling. "Easy."
"Who are you?" I asked.
"I'm Ari, I won't hurt you. Don't draw your weapon. Please forgive me, I didn't mean to startle you." I nodded, and she let go of me. "I was going to tell you that his three friends are right outside the door." I just stared at her, stared into her bright red eyes, which darkened as I watched, mesmerized. "Officer?" I blinked and jerked my eyes from her.
"Holy shit," Doris breathed. The entrance door opened, and Vincent and a paramedic walked in, directly over to us. The paramedic took over Doris's place, and she came to stand over me.
"Vendostrum," Vincent drawled. "You weren't supposed to shoot anyone."
"Well, excuse me if I shot someone in self-defense," I snapped, irritated by the mere presence of him. "What was I supposed to do? Spit at him?" The paramedic lifted Jose onto a stretcher and out the door.
"You were given orders."
"I was?" I asked. "Since when?" I slowly got to my feet and holstered my gun.
"Since I told you to be on security duty," he snapped.
"You told her to be on security duty?" Doris asked, looking paler than usual. She waved over herself, and then she waved at me. "Look at us, I'm in my SDPD uniform, and she is in black-ops, and you put her with me? Are you high? Because if you are, I'm going to have to report you to the chief."
"Angel Dust," I muttered under my breath. Doris's head snapped to me so fast her neck cracked.
"What did you say?"
"I said, didn't that hurt?" On my other side, Ari coughed. Damn, she heard that? I silently muttered.
"No, it felt good," she said, confused but for the moment, playing along.
"She was supposed to look after you," said Vincent.
"And that went very well," I said dryly. "As you can see, I did my job. Callahan is not lying in a pool of her own blood. Matter of fact, she didn't even faint." I winced as Doris elbowed me in my side, hard. Rubbing the sore spot, I glared down at her. "And don't ignore her question, are you high? Or drunk? Or-holy fuck!" I yelled, as the extremely pale guy moved in a blur. He grunted, and my ears rang at the sound of a gun being fired. Ari yanked me to the floor, and I pulled Doris down with me.
"Damn Peterson, I knew you were fucked in the head from the beginning!" I shouted. I gasped, and Doris finally fainted as the uh, nameless guy bared his two sets of fangs. I gulped and mentally shoved the fainting spell that wanted to come over me like a rushing wave of angry, dark churning water. "Did I say holy fuck?" I yelled.
"You did," Ari said from above me. "You may want to close your eyes for the next part."
"Oh, no, I am keeping them open," I said rapidly, my Swedish accent becoming more pronounced. I hit Doris on the head. "Wake the fuck up and give me that fifty bucks now." She came awake with a muffled scream, because my hand was clamped over her mouth.
"You're fired, Vendostrum!" Vincent shouted.
"Am I?" I shouted back at him. "Who the fuck are you to fucking fire me?" Doris finally fell silent, and I slowly took my hand from her mouth. Vincent's gun finally clicked empty, and he threw it at my direction. Ari's hand moved in the blink of an eye and caught it. The creepy guy, er, nameless, stepped aside. Doris couldn't take her eyes off him as he turned to face us, covered in bullet wounds. "Well?" I said to Vincent. Ari cleared her throat, and I looked at her.
"I'm sorry, but he can't talk." Doris moaned and again, fainted. I pinched myself and yelped at the pain. This was not a dream, then. "It's not a dream," Ari said slowly. Okay, you know what? That is just fucking creepy, and uh, intrusive, I silently grumbled. "My apologies." Damn it son of a mother holier than thou shit, I have gone insane. Ari's lips twitched, and I narrowed my eyes at her. She put up a hand. "All right all right, I'm out of your head, I promise." I grunted and looked at the nameless guy. He looked like he was in tremendous pain. Was it pain from the multiple bullet wounds? Or the pain of holding back from uh, eating someone? "Both," Ari answered helpfully. Hey! "I'm sorry, I'm sorry. I can't help it when you're projecting as you are." I sighed and pushed into a sitting position. I seriously need a drink, I thought and looked around the bar, this time, taking a closer look at everything.
"Don't punch me," Cane said from behind me. I looked at him, as he placed a cold drink in my hand.
"Oh, no," Ari said, moving away from me.
"We're all vampires here," Cane said and smirked. "And I assure you, this is not blood, I promise." I raised an eyebrow at him and took the ice-cold drink. He held his hand to Doris. "May I? I only wish to take you both to a table. This will be a very long night." I sighed and nodded. He took Doris from my lap, my eyes on him as I got up to follow. Cane put my partner into a booth and waited as I slid in beside her.
"Doris," I growled in her ear. "Wake up, damn it, and if you faint again, I swear I'll up the price." I sighed when she remained slumped over the table. I looked at my drink and scowled. It did smell like hard liquor, I thought and shrugged. I took a long swig and gasped, coughing. Yep, definitely alcohol. If it was spiked with blood, I couldn't taste it.
"Vendostrum, come in," a male voice crackled over my earpiece.
"Ah, shit," I groaned.
"Vendostrum, do you copy?" the voice asked a minute later when I didn't answer. Cane set a cold drink in front of my partner and put a hand on the back of her head. I stared wide-eyed, as she jolted awake with a gasp.
"I am not even going to ask," I muttered and took another swig of my drink.
"Vendostrum!" Doris reached a shaky hand to her collar and pressed a button.
"Carson!" she yelled. "If she doesn't answer, that means she's busy. Now if you don't mind, we have business to get back to." She dropped her hand to her drink and snorted. "Business my ass." Taking another swig, I sighed as the cold burn went down my throat.
"You're not going to faint on me again, are you?" I asked, staring at my partner. She shrugged and shoved her drink toward me. "Oh, come on," I said and shoved it back at her. "Drink up. By tomorrow morning, you won't even remember a single thing."
"According to who?"
"According to this brilliant alcohol of course."
"Of course," she said dryly and took a very, very long swig.
I again looked around the bar, realizing that Ari and the creepy ass dude were no longer here. "Where is Ari and uh, that dude?" I asked Cane. "And Vincent?"
"They? told me they'll be back, and they took Vincent with them."
I nodded rapidly and took another long pull of my drink. "I don't know if I should be scared, laugh, or shrug it off."
"I don't freaking believe it," Doris muttered into her glass.
"Oh, believe it," said Cane. "It is very real. I can erase your memory, and this night will cease to exist for you."
Doris's eyes widened. "You can do that?"
"He can," a deep male voice said from beside me, and I gasped, choking on my drink. I set my drink down, and someone thumped me on my back, and I took in a deep, burning breath.
"Oh, that hurts," I gasped.
"Forgive me."
"Don't mind him," said Ari.
"Yours was nothing," Doris wheezed, and I looked over to her.
"What?" I asked, staring at her, eyes streaming and nose running. "Oh," I said and coughed. "Nice trick, too bad I missed it." She glared at me and grabbed a wad of napkins from the center of the table. Someone tapped my shoulder, and I turned to find another vampire with bright red eyes and blonde hair smirking at me.
"Hi," she said cheerfully and held out her hand. When I didn't make a move to shake it, she grabbed my hand and shook it enthusiastically. "I'm Kira, and you are?"
"Um," I said hesitantly and grabbed my drink with my free hand and slammed it. Yep, my world spun as I drained my glass. I set the empty glass back on the table, and Kira dropped my hand, still smirking. Reaching over, I snatched Doris's drink and slammed it.
"Hey!" Doris exclaimed.
"Sorry," I slurred and looked to Cane. "Can I get another glass?"
Cane laughed. "I believe that is enough drinking for you."
"But." I slid from the booth, and the floor rushed up to meet me, but before I could face plant with it, a cold hand grabbed hold of my arm, steadying me and taking the empty glass I was holding from my unresisting hand. "Hey, let me go."
"Not likely, sweetheart." Oh, great, it was that creepy dude. Kira came into my blurred of a vision and waved her hand in front of my face.
"What's your name?" she asked.
"Um, what?" I asked, confused.
"Your name, what's your name?" I just stared at her. "Your name," she enunciated slowly. An arm came around me and hauled me up against a hard body.
"I think it is time for you both to go home," said Ari.
"Let me go, I can drive," I mumbled.
"Can you?" the creepy dude holding me asked. I nodded. "Shall we test your ability to drive?" I again nodded, as Kira reached into my pocket and pulled out my car keys. She reached to my ear and took out my earpiece, unclipping the mini microphone from the collar of my shirt.
"Hey, you can't do that," I grumbled at her.
Kira smiled, and inclining her head to me, she turned and headed for the bar entrance. "We'll meet again, officer," she said and stepped out into the night.
"Come back," I said halfheartedly.
"I believe it is time for you to sleep it off," the creepy dude growled in my ear.
"What are you??" I trailed off, as my world went black.

Chapter Two

TRISTAN

Bridget Vendostrum, a name repeated over and over in my head, as the scent of alcohol burned my nose and the back of my throat. Fuck me, and fuck me hard. Never thought, a Vendostrum would one day walk into a bar, and into the vampire world. Bridget pushed weakly against my arm. I sighed and willed open her front door, stepping over the threshold. "Let me go, god damn it," she slurred as I kicked the door shut and mentally locked it. Ignoring her, I walked down the short hallway to her bedroom and pushed open the door. "Nice job," I said to Ari, standing beside the bed. She moved out of the way as I stalked over to the bed and lowered Bridget onto it. Bridget groaned and holy hell, I prayed she wasn't going to throw up on me. I slowly removed my arm from under her and straightened, looking down at her, at her bloodshot eyes and alcohol fused gaze. I stood there, silent, as her eyes fluttered shut, and she fell into an alcohol induced coma. I took my eyes off of her and carefully unholstered her gun. As Ari's cool hand rested gently on my shoulder, I turned, feeling the brief buzz of Kira pulling up the driveway. A few minutes later, the front door opened, and she entered, dropping the keys on the small table just inside the door. I looked to the doorway as she appeared. I gestured her in, and she strode to the bureau, setting down the earpiece and looking at me. "Who is she?" she whispered, low enough that it wouldn't wake the human, drunk or not. I remained silent, having no idea where to even begin. Not even Ari knew my birth given name, and spouting something like, 'oh, you know, she is my great, times a billion, great granddaughter'. Kira smirked. "Is it a secret?" she asked and moved to my side. She elbowed me, and I winced. "Step aside; I'm going to make her more comfortable." Ari pulled me away from the bed, and I cross the small room to lean against a wall, the gun still in my hand. Glancing at it, I cursed, because it was still loaded, and the safety was off. With quick precision, I unloaded the glock 22 and walked over to her nightstand, setting both glock and magazine onto it. I turned to the sleeping human and scowled at her. "Get out of the room or turn around," Kira said to me. I gave her a questioning look. She sighed. "I'm going to strip her, and for the sake of her fragile mind, turn around or leave the room." Sighing, I turned and strode to the door. Closing it, I leaned against it, my eyes squeezed shut. My stomach clenched painfully, as my hunger grew. My lower set of fangs I was doing so great in keeping them sheathed for the past hour, extended to their full length. Damn it.
"I know that look," Ari whispered from directly in front of me. My eyes opened to meet her dark red ones. Her hand came up, and she poked a finger into my mouth. She pushed against one of my fangs, and I licked at it, drawing her finger further into my mouth. She yelped, as I bit down, puncturing it with one of my fangs. I didn't release her, until she smacked me upside the head. Ari huffed, licking closed the wound. I looked over to Kira, hands on her hips, and pouting. My head swam at the taste of Ari's blood, and my vision, already red, deepened.
"What?" I softly growled.
"I was hoping for an X-rated show," Kira whispered, smirking.
I walked over to her, pulling her into my arms and glaring down at her. "In your dreams," I whispered in her ear.
"I really don't want a show," she whispered, squirming as I nuzzled her neck, my mouth watering and fangs aching to sink into that soft skin of hers. "That's just?" She shuddered.
I chuckled. "Are we done here?" I asked. She nodded, and I teleported.
I dropped my arms from around her and jumped back, my hand flashing and catching Jordana around the throat. The vampire snarled, and Kira ducked and dodged the side kick aiming for her. I pulled Jordana to me and held her struggling body tightly against mine. I flashed across the Council's lounge and slammed her into the wall. She let out a startled gasp, her eyes slowly focusing on me. "What was that for?" she asked brightly, and I let her pry my fingers from around her neck.
"Not in a good mood, are you?" I asked dryly.
She raised an eyebrow at me. "I'm always in a good mood. Why wouldn't I be?"
"You almost kicked me in the head," Kira grumbled from her position by the door leading out of the lounge.
"Damn," Ari huffed from the other side of the door. It opened, and she strode in. "Why do I always miss the fun? It is not fair, you know?"
"Ella," Jordana sang, and I smiled, as Ari gave a horrified gasp.
"Jordana!" Ari exclaimed. She stopped beside me and glared at the crazed vampire. Jordana stared at her, blinking, her smile turning into a grin. "Don't call me that," she growled.
"Why not? Don't you like?"
"Fine, no brains for you for a day."
Jordana's grin turned into a pout. "But."
"You call me Ella again, and you won't have any brains for two days."
"But."
"So, if you call me by that name ten times, you won't get any brains for ten days, got it? The more you call me Ella, the more days you go without brains." Jordana's eyes went out of focus, and the bright red bled from her eyes faster than you could say, 'oh shit'. "You're handling this one," she said to me and flashed from the lounge. "I handled her last night and the night before," she continued, closing the door behind her. I sighed, as growls ripped from Jordana. She may be three hundred and twenty-two years old, but she was faster and stronger than your ordinary average fledgling. Three months ago, I found out that for every brain she consumed, she gained the victim's strength and agility, along with their memories, both good and bad. And she showed that fact by shoving me across the room. Kira gasped and disappeared into the Council chamber as I got up and flashed after Jordana. I caught her, and she hissed, baring her fangs to strike. I threw her to the floor before she could bite me. There was no way in hell I was going to let her sink those fangs into me and then have venom course through my bloodstream. Yes, I could rid myself of the poison, any vampire could, but I wasn't your average normal vampire, was I? Jordana could no longer control the releasing of venom when she fed. Maybe she could control it, but I hadn't seen her doing so, or she didn't care to try it. So it was blood bags for her, or supervised hunts. A dose of the venom in humans was agonizingly painful, and sometimes, deadly. In her case, sometimes was every time, as I found out, a night after her re-sire-ing by Liana and Sven. She banged her head against the floor, hissing. With a mental push, I forced her to retract her fangs, and she screeched when she couldn't extend them to their full length. She snapped at me, and I growled. Hot and cold waves of sensation coursed through me, and I gritted my teeth.
"You're hungry," Jordana observed and again, snapped her teeth at me. I winced as the light fixture over my head came crashing down on me.
"Stop," I growled, cursing as a doorknob-where the hell did that come from-smacked me upside the head. Fuck did that hurt.
"Are you going to compel me?" she hissed.
"No," I said slowly. "I want you to stop on your own." I dove inside her head and grimaced.
She giggled. "This again?" she asked, and I grunted as she slammed me out. I stared deeply into her semi-focused eyes and sighed. I couldn't hear her thoughts. Well, I could, but it was like listening to an un-tuned radio, full of static and words I couldn't make out. Sometimes I could, but most of the times I couldn't, especially when she was in her own little world which was eighty percent of the times, and to me, that was? very disconcerting. Without hurting her mind even more than it already was, I couldn't go deeper to read. And all I saw inside her mind was a black void. Jordana sighed and went limp. I stiffened, because that was a very bad sign.
"Jordana," I warned.
Her eyes widened in surprise. "What?" I jerked to the side as something sharp slammed into me. "Got you," she sang and wriggled from under me. I turned my head to the left and snarled when I saw a freaking sword sticking out of my side. Jordana squealed, and I gave her a murderous look. Half laughing, half gasping, she ran from the lounge. Chapter Five

BRIDGET

This is all just a dream, I silently muttered to myself. This is all just a nightmare, and I'm going to wake up, anytime soon now. I watched, as a team of officers directed traffic away from the massacre, and yes it was a massacre. The four extremely pale figures standing in the shadows didn't miss a thing, as their eyes tracked each officer's every move. A shudder ran through me as one of them looked my way. Panic suddenly came over me, fast and hard. The hand around my arm tightened painfully, and someone choked. I reached for my gun, but before I could draw it, another cold hand locked around my wrist.

I again bit my bottom lip, making it bleed again. She stiffened, and I jerked from her. This time I made it to my patrol car, but before I could get in, someone grabbed me and gently spun me around. I thought my heart was going to explode from my chest. At the rate it was pounding, I was surprised it wasn't five feet away by now. I looked at the creepy guy from the bar, and I tried to swallow past my constricted airway.

"Will you be able to handle the fact that vampires really do exist?"

He smiled tightly and nodded. "Go to dinner with Astrid." In my head, I was freaking out. How the hell did he know I was going to meet up with my sister for dinner? "I'll pay you a visit, if not tonight, tomorrow night. I'll answer any questions you have. You will remember this moment, but until then, keep it all to yourself." He stepped back from me, and it actually looked painful for him to do so. "Go on, do whatever you were going to do," he said, and I blinked. I looked around. There was no one here. What the hell? I thought. Shaking my head, I turned to my car, and got in.

ARI

Chapter Six

LORENA

"Have you come to kill the humans?" Violet asked in a low tone.
I turned to the irritating huntress and gave her an annoyed look. "How many times have you asked that over the years?"
"Many times," she hissed.
"If you ask that one more time, I'm going to stab you in your sleep," I snarled. "And if you think I'm fucking around, you better think twice. And for the record, I don't give a fuck who your sire is."
Violet glared at me. "I swear," she said through gritted teeth. "One day, I'm going to show you what I can do with my death magic," she hissed.

Chapter Eight

I stabbed a finger into his chest, and my hands tingled with magic. "I'll? I'll come up with a spell to make your brain explode out of your ass!" I snapped. The arrogant ass got the nerve to laugh at me. "What? You don't believe I can?"
He dropped his hands from me and flashed his fangs. "Oh, I don't doubt that you can, sweetheart." I squeaked as the only dim light bulb in the room went out. I stumbled backward as mind numbing cold blast into me. Jordana, the bitch, laughed as I hit the floor, shivering.
"What are-" I broke off with a gasp. "What are you doing?" I struggled as I felt my magic draining from me. "Stop it! Stop it! You can't do this! How are you doing this?"
"Oh, you poor, poor witch," Jordana said sweetly.
"Tell me, Davina," said Sven. "Have you ever wondered what it's like to live without your magic?"
"You can't do this," I said and almost cried in relief when the draining abruptly stopped. I was extremely low on magic, but having some was better than none. One casting of a major spell would surely drain me completely.
"Oh," Sven said softly, and I let out a squeak at how close he was. Shit, I didn't even hear him move. "You have no idea what I can, or can't do. And, you didn't answer my question."
I let out a huff. "Yes," I grudgingly admitted. "I have."
He chuckled. "So have I," he whispered. "I wondered what it is like to be human again. Five thousand years as vampire overshadows my thirty years of my very short, short human life. I barely remember anything from my days as a human."
My breath caught in my throat, and my heart pounded loud in my ears. "You're not Sven," I breathed.
"Ding-ding-ding-ding-ding," Jordana said cheerfully. "Congratulation, you just won yourself a seven-day, six-night getaway to a tropical location of your choosing!" she exclaimed in an imitation of a game show host.
"You're not Sven," I repeated and mentally smacked myself for not noticing it earlier. Stupid, stupid, stupid!
"What gave it away?" Sven asked in amusement.
I shrugged. "Does it matter?"
"No, it doesn't." I stiffened as I heard Carolyn groaning. "Are you going to cooperate, Davina? Or, do I have to hurt your sweet, precious daughter?"
I gulped. "Don't you dare lay a finger on her."
"Mom?" I closed my eyes, wondering how I got myself into this mess. "What's going on?"
"As Jailyn so well put it, you need to keep a tighter leash on your witches," Sven coolly reminded me. "So, what shall it be? Cooperate? Or?" Carolyn yelped, and I cursed.
"Don't hurt her. Please, don't hurt her."
"I won't, if you give me what I want."
"The other elders will be looking for me."
"Oh, I believe they already are."
"Jordana, no," Jailyn growled, and I let out a small scream as cold hands wrapped around my throat and lifted me off the floor. I kicked out and connected with a body part. Jordana grunted, and I sucked in a pained breath as she slammed me against a wall. A low growl escaped her, and I cringed as I felt her breath against my neck. Her hold tightened, and I struggled to breathe.
"Does this hurt, witch?" she purred in my ear. "Does it hurt to breathe?"
"Yes," I wheezed. "Look, Jordana, I'm sorry for what happened-"
"Are you?" she hissed, and white light exploded before my eyes as she bashed my head into the wall. "Are you really?"
"Jordana!" Sven said sharply. "Enough!" She released me, and I slid to the floor, gasping and moaning.
"Why," she snarled. "Won't you let me kill her?"
"I understand your hatred for witches, but we need her alive, sweetheart."
"You don't understand shit!" A door slammed, and Jordana's screams of outrage quickly died off as she moved further away. Sven sighed, and I continued to slowly take in air through my semi-crushed windpipe.
"Go after her," said Jailyn. "I got it from here, and don't worry, I will get answers out of her." I cried out and curled into myself as what felt like being ripped in two came over me. "You, have my word."

JORDANA

I stomped up the stairs, seething and seeing red. I slammed open Tristan's fortified door and continued up another flight of stairs. Cursing and screaming, I ran up four more flights of stairs before stopping at the last door. I banged on the steel door with my fists, hard enough to split knuckles. Pausing, he slipped on his sunglasses before opening the front door. My world fragmented, and I blinked. Sven put a hand on the back of my neck and led me outside and into the shades of trees. A pained look flashed in his eyes, and he sighed, pulling me into his arms. Burying my face in the hollow of his neck, I sighed.
"You smell like Tristan. Did you have sex with him?" I giggled as he stiffened.
"Please tell me you did not just ask me that."
I laughed. "I did."

"Wait," he whispered in my ear. "Wait."
"For what?"
"What is one of the rules of being a hunter?"

"Good girl." He ran his hand up and down my back in a soothing manner. "Stay very still for me. Can you do that?" I reluctantly nodded. He stilled. "Good, I'll let you do the catching, but first, we see what he's doing around this area."
"Promise?"
"I promise, and then you and I, will go witch hunting."
I grinned evilly. "About fucking time." Chuckling, and with me still in his arms, my sire teleported.

Chapter Sixteen

LORENA

I surfaced from what felt like a cold sticky spider web of darkness. I blinked and looked around, the gentle breeze of the cold wind lifting my hair slightly from my neck. All around me was nothing but? ice? Turning, I scanned the icy landscape stupidly. Was I actually dreaming, or had my power gone haywire while I was sleeping? I yelped as my surrounding evolved itself into a? beach? I stared incredulously at the white sand, hearing the sound of crashing waves in the distance as the sun beat down on my neck. Shaking my head, I thought of woods, and trees, and the night sky, and was rewarded as my surrounding once again shuddered and changed. I looked around, and nodded at the huge trees around me. Better, I thought and stared up at the stars. I heard a sigh coming from behind me, and I spun around, peering into the trees and beyond, seeing nothing. "Exactly."

I can't go a day without drinking two, at least two pints of your blood, and mind you, your," I continued, putting emphasis on the word 'your.' "Blood so that my stomach doesn't feel like it is being melted by acid. I tried drinking from other vampires, and you know how ineffective that turned out." Ari and Jailyn are snatching witches left and right and center, and Adalyn is off doing who knows what with that Alek guy. Sven and Jordana are on a witch hunt to Jordana's delight. Especially that fucking bitch ass of a fucking tramp? If the whole vampire community found out what happened, there's going to be a fucking riot, and I don't even want to think about that." When you and the others come for me, do not awaken me until you know that I am secured away from civilization. Do not, and I repeat, do not wake me the moment you come for me. He was clearly starved out of his mind, but at least ten percent of him was back online. His eyes finally landed on me, and Casiar quickly removed his hand from my shoulder. Luckily the pain didn't reappear. Maybe more than ten percent of him was back, or Casiar muttered a two seconds pain numbing spell or something. Hoping that he wasn't going to kill me, I walked over to him, stopping out of grabbing range.
"Tristan?" I said softly. The chains clinked against each other as he moved, the only sound breaking the silence apart from his harsh ragged pants. I looked back to Casiar, giving him a questioning look. He came over to me, a clear plastic cup appearing in his hand. I blinked at it, as he stopped beside me. He held out the cup to me and nodded to my hand.
"Unless you want to risk him chewing off your hand literally, I recommend bloodletting into the cup. I'd help you, but I like my head right where it is at the moment." Nodding in sudden understanding, I took the cup from him. Mates, whether it was vampires, demons, or shifters, were very territorial. Usually a mate didn't mind the opposite sex touching his or her partner, but at the moment? Casiar winced, quickly backing away from me. "And I prefer what's left of my functioning brain to remain intact." The necromancer gestured everyone back a safe distance and nodded to the cup in my hand. "Go on." Taking a deep breath, I ripped into my wrist, letting my blood fill the cup and quickly backing away as Tristan slammed against his chains. He screamed and cursed as I tear into my wrist a second time, his eyes fixed on the blood like it was chocolate. The cup filled to the brim, I walked back to him. He continued struggling, straining to break free.
"Tristan," I said and pressed the cup to his mouth. He stilled, inhaling deeply. His eyes went unfocused, and I pulled the cup away before he could eat the plastic along with the blood. Growling and faster than I could blink, he snatched the cup from my hand, some blood spilling over the edge. I looked down and noticed one of his hands wasn't chained to the pillar. Hissing, he downed the blood in one gulp, shuddering as the blood coursed through his body. Allia appeared beside him and held out her wrist, taking the empty cup from his hand. He let out a snarl, and Allia stiffened as his fangs sank in deep. Looking highly agitated, Tristan pulled back, only to yank her to him and sinking his fangs into her jugular. Allia swore viciously under her breath as he continued to pull deeply on her neck. After a long minute or two, she ripped herself from him, stumbling into Riordan. The necromancer caught her and leaned in to close the wound before straightening and taking his turn in feeding Tristan. For the next half hour, and one by one, his siblings fed him, oldest to youngest. When they were done, Tristan finally slipped into a healing coma.
"That went better than I thought," Evelyn said cheerfully as she unchained him, and he fell into my arms. I grunted, holding all of his weight as I carried him away from the pillar.
"Hey." We all spun around, and I blinked, as Ian waved to us with a transparent hand.
"Ian?" Evelyn yelped. "You look? happy to be dead."
"I'm not," Ian grumbled. "But I'm not going to be all doom and gloom about it." Then he looked to Tristan in my arms. "Will he be okay?" he whispered, an anguished look in his eyes. He floated over to me and put a hand on his sire's back. "Shit," he muttered. "He's going to-" He jerked his hand away, and I froze, as Tristan went rigid. The conversations that were going on suddenly stopped, as all eyes focused on him. Guess he wasn't in a healing coma after all, I silently muttered. Tristan straightened and pulled away from me, his eyes clouded with pain and confusion. He looked to Ian and blinked. "I'm sorry," Ian said quietly. Retracting his claws, Tristan held up his hand.
"Why are you sorry?" he rasped, speaking out loud for the first time since his awakening.
"For dying," Ian said simply. "You still need to heal," he continued slowly. "And? do you mind putting some clothes on? I'm going blind."
"Everyone here barely has clothes on, and you're complaining," Tristan drawled, and then he groaned as his nose began to bleed. We watched as something past telepathically between the two of them, and I wondered what they were talking about, or reminiscing about. Ian nodded sadly and reached out to Jailyn, the closest vampire and necromancer to him.
"Sire," said Ian. "Kill that fucking bitch for me." Hisses, growls, and snarls rang throughout the abyss, echoing eerily through the wide, wide opened space of nothing. No one needed to ask who the bitch Ian was talking about, because everyone here knew that the bitch was none other than Shae.
"Oh," Tristan said, his voice no more than a deadly promise. "I will."
Ian smirked and nodded. "And as to how I died, my head was halfway severed when Ari and Alexander found me."
"Fuck!" I shouted and moved closer to him. Tristan's arm came around me before I could go through Ian. Still, I struggled. Both of us wet and sticky with blood all over, he still held me with no effort. His other arm came around me, trapping me against his chest. "How did we not know?" I asked angrily.
Ian held up both hands. "I was completely covered in blood, and you probably didn't see all of me. Besides, there were four shifters in the room with me. They're not stupid even though we like to think they are. One or more of them were probably blocking half of me from view."
"That is no excuse!" I seethed, Tristan groaning softly behind me as I continued to struggle.
"Look," Ian said with a sigh. "Don't blame yourself for my death." He looked around at all of us and scowled at Jailyn who had a guilty look on her face. "None of you," he said firmly.
"Easier said than done," Jailyn muttered. "If I hadn't released my souls on those bastards?"
Ian sighed. "You were pissed off. Even I knew that much in my half-conscious state. And sire, don't you dare say this was your fault, or I'm going to haunt you for eternity. I can do it too, you know."
"Go," Tristan said gently. I finally stopped struggling and went limp in his arms, the anger draining from me.
"Will you be okay? I mean, you won't go rogue, will you?" Everybody there? winced. Tristan sighed into my hair. "You won't turn rogue, right?" Ian pushed a nervous edge to his voice.
"I won't turn rogue," Tristan finally said. "But if I do, everyone around you here knows what is to be done."
"You can't be killed."
Tristan chuckled. "Sure I can, my child. But for the sake of the entire vampire race, I can be put to sleep." Looking unhappy, Ian nodded.
"And," said Evelyn. "If he's one step away from becoming a rogue, he has us to beat his ass back to his senses, like we have always done for the past? how long now?"
"How very touching, sister."
"Well, I tried to be."
"Okay," Ian grumbled.
"Go," Tristan said again. "I'll be fine." Jailyn took Ian's hand into hers and slowly led him away.
"I'll be watching over you," Ian muttered to himself as Jailyn hugged him to her and disappeared in a blinding white light.
"Damn it," I moaned. "This sucks balls." I straightened and turned in Tristan's arms. His nose was still bleeding, and I grimaced, pulling away from him. His eyes once again went dazed and unfocused. Evelyn lunged, catching him as he passed out, the blood vessels in his eyes bursting.
"Oh, dearest brother, you poor thing," Evelyn whispered, stroking his cold cheek. "Sleep, brother of mine, sleep."
I reached out and ran my fingers through his short hair. "Sleep, Tristan," I said softly. "I'll be here when you wake."
Evelyn looked over to Casiar and sighed. "I think we're done here. If you please, jump us." Casiar stared at Tristan for a very, very long time before nodding. I gasped as my stomach dropped, and everything went dark.

Chapter Twenty-three

LIANA

"Adaira," Jordana said with a pout. Adaira, the witch responsible for putting Tristan in a world of hurt, lay motionless on the cold stone floor of my basement. For over three hours, she showed no sign of waking up. I looked at the lithium blade on the table in front of me and picked it up.
"You know, Jordana," I said, frowning at the white blade with strange shimmer of silver to it when reflected by light. "I'm surprised she didn't combust into flames when you stabbed her. Maybe you should give her some more of your blood." After Evelyn had teleported us out of the fight, which by the way, I so wanted a part in, Jordana yanked the blade out and using the same blade, slashed open her wrist and force-fed the witch, healing her. For the next hour while waiting for Adaira to wake up, and the others to returned, I was freaking out, because no vampire had ever used a weapon that could zap a witch of her magic. Yes it wasn't a blade to weaken vampires, but still. So, now here I was, not letting my insane child near it as she continued to eye the thing like it was the most treasured weapon in the world. Technically it was, and I still couldn't wrap my head around the fact that Brulia, out of all the witches in the state of California, had given it to me. Davina was soooo going to have her head for this.
"It's magical. Isn't-?" She screamed as I dropped the blade and moved in a blur, my hand clamped tightly over her mouth.
"Careful, sweetie," I whispered. Jordana's eyes widened, and she nodded. "I know she's not awake, but you never know, so shhhh." She again nodded. I removed my hand and went back to my chair and slowly sat.
"I'm sorry," she mumbled.
"Don't be," I said and picked the blade back up. "You think if I stab her, she'll wake up?"
Jordana laughed. "Worth a shot."
"No, let's not test that," Sven said from the top of the stairs.
"You're back," I said, setting the blade down on the table and getting to my feet.
"Been back for a while now."
I flashed up the stairs and stopped before him, looking him up and down. "How did it go?"
"Better than I hoped," he said, looking past me to Jordana. "How's everything here?" he asked, pulling me into his arms.
I rested my head on his shoulder and sighed. "She won't wake up."
"Hmm," he said thoughtfully. "Did you give Brulia a call?"
"I did, but she hadn't answered her phone."
"Maybe it will take twelve hours for her to wake up," said Jordana.
"Maybe," said Sven. Jordana was suddenly beside us, and she pushed her way between me and Sven, forcing us apart.
"Jordana?" I asked nervously.
"Where is Tristan?"
"He's in one of the guest rooms," Sven said and glanced at the opened door behind him. "Would you like to see him?"
"Can I?" she asked sadly, and I inwardly winced.
"Come," he said and turned. My hand resting on Jordana's back, we followed Sven as he led us through the kitchen, the living room, up a flight of stairs, and turning right down the hall. The air felt charged, and I wondered if Tristan was awake or not. Stopping before a door, Sven put his hand on the doorknob and paused.
"How long have you guys been back?" I asked.
"About an hour and a half."
"He's probably awake," I said with a sigh.
"He is," Ari said from inside the room. "Turn off the light before you come in." I looked to Sven in question.
"He no longer has the wristband Brulia gave him," he said and glanced up at the light, scowling. A moment later, the hall was plunged into complete darkness. Then he turned the knob and pushed open the door. At the sight of Tristan chained to the bed, Jordana let out a moan. She flashed into the room, dropping heavily onto the bed. She just? stared at him, and he just? stared impassively back at her. "Thank the world that you are not naked," Sven said dryly, stepping into the room. I followed him in and closed the door behind me. Ari too, was on the bed, casually stroking Tristan's cheek. I was a little surprised he didn't turn his head and bite off her fingers.
"Does it still hurt?" Jordana asked in a small voice, tentatively touching the chain over his wrist.
"I have a fucking migraine," Tristan groaned and closed his eyes.
"You need to heal," Ari said disapprovingly. "You keep waking up every?" She scowled. "Ten minutes."
"I do not," he said with a weary sigh.
Ari stopped her stroking and glared at him. "You do too," she growled. "Now stop being a stubborn ass and go to sleep."
"How long are you demanding I sleep?" he asked dryly.
"Eighteen hours."
"I only need twelve."
"Eighteen," she said firmly, and I hid a smile.
"There's no need-"
"Don't argue with me," she said sharply, cutting him off. "You need to heal, and the way to go about that is for you to sleep deeply."
"Yes, dear," Tristan said with a heavy sigh. "If you insist."
She leaned down and kissed him. "I insist," she whispered. "It will be around seven in the evening when you wake up."
Tristan nodded. "And Jordana, my sweet insane youngling?"
Jordana leaned closer to him. "Yes?" she asked softly.
"Please don't kill Adaira. She and I? have unfinished business between us."
Jordana patted him on the stomach. "I promise I won't kill her." She pouted. "But can I still eat her?"
He chuckled. "As long as you don't kill her."
She nodded. "Got it." And with me standing by the door, Sven standing beside the bed, and Ari and Jordana leaning over him, Tristan let out a long breath. The charge in the air slowly dissipated, as he slipped into unconsciousness.
"Damn woman," I said, smirking as Ari let out a relieved sigh and sat back on the bed. "Leave it to you to freely order him around without fear that he'll rip your head off before you could finish your demands."
Ari shrugged. "I know he won't hurt me. Well, at least not on purpose." There was a knock on the door, and I stepped aside as it opened to allow Evelyn and Casiar into the room. Shifting uneasily and her head down, Jordana slipped off the bed and flashed to a corner of the room and stood motionless, her expression going blank. Ari glared at the necromancer. "Are you here to add another layer of magic on him?"
"No," Casiar said, his hands raised and backing up a step from Ari, who had murderous intent in her eyes. "I only came to let you know that there are ten humans on standby. He needs to be fed every two hours."
"Oh," she said, relaxing a tiny bit, and then she frowned. "Two hours? I thought he needed to feed every six."
"That would be true if he wasn't healing. And speaking of feeding?" He glanced at Evelyn and vanished.
Ari glared at the spot where Casiar was a second ago and growled in frustration. "I really, really hate him at the moment."
Evelyn chuckled and sat down beside her. "I know," she said, giving Ari's arm a light squeeze. "But he is only helping, not hindering."
"I know," Ari said with a sigh. "But still."
Evelyn took the clearly agitated vampire into her arms and patted her back in a soothing manner. "The magic is not hurting him at all. I can promise you that," she whispered. "You would know it if it hurts him." A hand landed on my shoulder, and I looked up to find Sven who was discreetly pulling Jordana from her corner as Evelyn continued to soothe Ari's frayed nerves. With a nod to Evelyn, he teleported us from the room.

JADE

The morning breeze was cool and refreshing, as I took in my surroundings. The streets were quiet, a few stragglers making their way to wherever they were going. Leaves crunched loudly to my sensitive hearing as I stepped further into the shadows. The two buildings on either side of me were decrepit and smelled of mildew and rotting woods. The light pole on the corner of the street flickered on and off as I scented the air. A couple of homeless humans eyed me strangely from behind the dumpster and cardboard boxes, but they remained silent for which I was very grateful. Nodding to myself, I stepped back onto the street, dodging cars as the occupant's honk their horns at me, making me cringe. Once out of sight behind a clump of trees, I launched myself into the sky. Not soon after I was airborne, I sensed the presence of another vampire. When I was high enough to be undetectable by humans, I turned. "Skyler?" I asked in surprise. "What are you doing out and about?"
"Hunting," she said with a sigh. "But I don't want to feed on the homeless. Their blood isn't so? great."
I smirked. "Don't like drug-laced blood?" Skyler grunted as she hovered an arm's length from me, the wind around us cold and biting. "Ever thought about breaking in and feeding from a sleeping human?"
"I have, but?"
I held out my hand to her, and she put her icy one into mine. "Come, let's find you breakfast." Skyler's eyes widened, just before a sharp pain ripped through me.
"Jade," she said in a strangled voice as rage overrode the pain in my back. Did someone just plunge a fucking knife into my back? Gritting my teeth, I jerked my hand from Skyler, and then I was freefalling as another blade struck my spinal cord.
"Skyler don't!" I yelled as the panicked fledgling streaked across the sky. Oh, this was going to hurt, I thought as the ground rushed up to meet me. Before I became a pancake upon the ground, Skyler's arms came around me.
"Sorry!" she yelled as I gasped in pain, the two blades going deeper into my back. The scent of fear in my nose, the fledgling flew high and fast as my body tried to dislodge the foreign objects that didn't belong. Breathing shallowly, Skyler turned me in her arms until I met her pitched black eyes. "Should I pull them out?" she asked, the scent of fear rising from her.
"Just fly," I gasped, and then blinked at Elijah who appeared in midair behind Skyler.
"No need to go any farther," he growled and caught both of us before a startled Skyler could drop me. Then everything went dark.
I didn't even have time to figure out where I was before Ari was on us. She sent Elijah crashing into a wall, and if I wasn't in so much pain, I'd laugh my ass off. "Skyler!" she said, breathing hard like her child was doing at the moment. I painfully hit the floor on my back and silently cursed. "What happened? Are you hurt? Where were you?" And then she looked at me. She pressed her fingers into her temples and moaned. "Just fucking shoot me, please?" She knelt beside me, and it looked like she was either going to bang her head against something solid, kill someone, cry, or all three. "Sorry, Jade," she said tiredly.
"Don't apologize, just take them out," I said, giving her a pained smile. She rolled me onto my stomach, muttering under her breath. Elijah, who remained in an awkward heap, grunt and got slowly to his feet, rubbing his head. He held up his hand before Ari could apologize to him too. He disappeared into thin air as Skyler knelt beside Ari, putting her hand on my back.
"It's not my blood," she reassured her sire.
Ari sighed. "I know." Without any warning, the two blades were yanked from me. I sucked in a sharp breath, letting it out with a curse. Then I froze, as my back began to tingle, or more precisely, my wounds. Ari went very still, and I wondered what in the world was happening to me. I grunted as my shirt unstuck from my back, and then cold hands, more likely Skyler's covered the two opened wounds. The feeling of magic was suddenly in the air, and I stiffened.
"Skyler, what are you doing?" I asked, a hint of warning in my voice.
"Relax," she said grumpily. "This never worked before." I twitched as I felt my wounds begin to nit back together. A few seconds later, Skyler removed her hands and let out a harrumph. The pain now gone and no longer bleeding all over the place, I slowly moved into a sitting position and looked at Skyler.
"Cool," she said and stared at the blood on her hands. "It actually worked."
Ari smirked and patted her on the head. "That is because once you became a vampire, your magic came to life, fully."
"And now I don't know how to control my magic," Skyler muttered, fear gone now that no one was dying. "I think I almost accidentally staked Jailyn a week ago."
"Really?" I asked, getting to my feet. "Damn, wish I'd been there to see it."
"It wasn't that amusing."
"It sure as hell would've been for me."
She snorted and got to her feet. "I bet," she said dryly and headed for the kitchen. Sighing, I followed her. Stopping at the fridge, she opened it and peeked inside. She pulled out a couple of blood bags and slammed shut the door. I walked to the pristine white counter and leaned on it, watching her as she popped the blood into the microwave. A few seconds later and before the black box could ding, she pushed the button, opening the door. Pulling out the bags and leaving the door opened, she walked over to me. "Want one?" she asked. I nodded and took the hot plastic from her and bit into it. Wincing from the temperature, I almost groaned out loud as I drained it.
"Well," Ari said from the archway leading back into the living room. She came in and stopped before Skyler. She frowned. "Have another one," she said as her child pulled the empty blood bag from her mouth.
"But there's only three left."
Ari winced. "I'll be back with a few more," she said and flashed from the kitchen.
"What was she going to say before she came in?" Skyler asked.
I shrugged. "You're asking me?"
"Hey, you know her better than I do."
"I was going to ask if you saw who attacked you, Jade," Ari said from down the hall somewhere. A moment later, she appeared in the kitchen and dropped four more bags of the red liquid on the counter beside me.
"Are all those for me?" Skyler asked and snatched a couple from the counter and ripped into one.
Ari stared at Skyler intently, causing the fledgling to shift uncomfortably. "How long have you gone without feeding?"
Looking thoughtful, Skyler drained the blood and frowned, dropping the empty bag into her sire's outstretched hand. "A day and a half? I think?" she mumbled. Ari sighed. "I'm not really into drinking from plastic bag," she muttered.
"I can take her hunting with me," I offered. "I won't mind having a hunting partner." I put up a hand when Ari turned to me. "I give you my word that I won't let anything happen to her," I said quickly. "I'll even swear it by blood if you want."
"Stop," Ari said, shaking her head. "Stop, a word bind is good enough."
"Oh, thank the lord and Jesus," I said in relief. At this, Skyler choked and spewed blood from her mouth as she burst out laughing and coughing. I smiled and tried not to join in with her, though it was hard as hell.
"Er? okay then," Ari said slowly.
"Don't worry," I said dryly. "I don't worship the guy. Just a saying, you know?" Ari laughed softly and nodded.
"Thanks, Jade," said Skyler. "Thanks a whole lot," she grumbled and stared at the blood on the linoleum floor. "Now I have to clean it up."
"No need," said Ari. "I got it. You just go and clean yourself up."
Skyler nodded. "Can I see Tristan after?"
Ari hesitated. "Sure," she said slowly. "But if he so much as even twitches a finger, you flash from that room and let me know." She nodded. "No hesitating," she warned. "If he lays a finger on you, you're done for."
"I know, sire. I know." And with that, Skyler was gone.

Chapter Twenty-four

ADAIRA

As if someone had dunk me in ice cold water, I painfully sucked in a lungful of air, gasping. What the hell was wrong with me? I thought, and then it all came rushing back to me in a painful wave of memories, the battle with the vampires, being stabbed in the back, and then? nothing. How long was I out? I opened my eyes to find utter and complete darkness. Where in the hell was I? "Anyone there?" I asked nothing but darkness.
"If you have to ask that," a young female voice said. "You're stupider than I thought."
"Who the hell are you?"
"Why is that always the first question out of everyone's mouth?" a deep male voice growled.
The female snorted. "Wouldn't you ask the same thing?" she asked.
"No, I'd be going for their throat."
"Of course," she said with a sigh. "Adaira," she suddenly said in a cheerful tone. "First, I'm Kira, and you're deep within the Vampiric Council HQ. So, I tell you now, don't try any subtle moves. Or? you'll regret it, dearly."
"Why so cheerful?" I muttered. There was a loud crack, and the room was suddenly bathed in a green glow. I looked around, and found a blonde vampire holding a glow stick. She smiled at me and waved it in the air.
"Do you remember they used to sell a bunch of this in stores everywhere?" She looked thoughtful. "Wonder why they don't anymore. You know I'd freeze a bunch of these and warm them up in the microwave to make them glow brighter. Well, until I warmed one a little too long. When I took it out, the stupid glowstick literally broke open on me. Some of the red liquid got into my mouth. It tasted disgusting, and I honestly thought I was going to die." She muttered something under her breath. "But enough of that," she said and dropped the green stick on the floor. "You're probably wondering how long you've been out. Well, your ass was in sweet oblivion for three days. Who knew a lithium blade could put out a witch for that long? What I'm wondering is, do you have your magic back?"
"Why do you want to know?"
She shrugged. "Just curious."
"If I did have my magic, I wouldn't tell you."
She sighed. "If I were you, I start talking."
"And if I don't?"
She again sighed. "You know what?" she asked, looking at whoever I couldn't see past the green glow. "How about you take over? I suck." A low chuckle floated from the shadows, and I gritted my teeth. It was all I could do not to squirm.
"What is this about?" I asked. "Why am I here?"
Kira gave me an icy stare so chilling that for a second, my brain practically rattled in my skull. "You," she growled. "Need to ask that fucking question?" Then, I couldn't breathe, as she grabbed me by the neck and yanked me to my feet, slamming me against the unyielding wall behind me. White light exploded behind my eyes as pain ripped throughout my entire body. "You put my sire's brain on fire, and you're asking what is this about?" she snarled. "Really?" she hissed as I struggled to breathe. "Really?"
"Careful, sweetheart. She's turning a lovely shade of blue." Growling under her breath and her arm trembling, she slowly released me and backed away. I gasped in air, doubling over, wheezing as I massage my throat. Shit, that was going to leave bruises in a few hours, probably in a few seconds.
"If you puke, I'm going to make you eat it," she snapped as I slowly straightened.
"Who's your sire?" I wheezed.
"Who do you think?" she drawled. "Who were you trying to kill just these past oh? I don't know, week?"
I suddenly went cold all over. "He's here?" I rasped and strained my eyes to see into the shadows just beyond the stupid glow stick. Kira bent and picked up the only light source in the room and dropped it into her pocket, plunging the room to almost complete darkness. There was a knock, and I heard a door opening.
"Kira?" another female voice asked, and it was a voice I knew too well.
"I'm in here, Davina."
"Davina," I yelped. "Davina, you have to get me out of here," I said and took a step toward the stairs backlit by the light coming from the opened door. "Please?" I stumbled to a stop as a warning tingle crept down my spine.
"Not so fast," Kira said, back to her cheerful tone. "You're not done here."
"I am so-" I gasped as I felt a cold sharp stinging pain in my neck. I choked and gurgled as hot blood poured from my neck wound. She slit my throat, I thought dazedly. That bitch fucking slit opened my throat. Panicked, I reached deep into myself and broke out into a cold sweat when I couldn't feel the stored energy of my magic. I dropped to my knees as the room began to spin around me. They really stabbed me with a lithium blade, I thought. Why else couldn't I access my magic? I had no magic to heal myself, and I was going to die via blood loss. Just? wonderful.

KIRA

"Kira," Tristan groaned. The air stirred, and he was suddenly in front of the dying witch. He pulled her to her feet and tilted her head back as she continued to choke on her own blood. With a growl, his tongue flicked out, and I sighed as he began to heal the bitch. Shuddering in pleasure, he stepped back from her and let her dropped weakly to the blood-coated floor.
"Wow," I said. "You didn't eat her."
"Kira!" Davina suddenly exclaimed. "Why did you do that for?"
I shrugged. "She wouldn't answer me when I asked if she got her magic back, so I had to find out in some other ways. And now, I have my answer."
She sighed. "You could've asked me," she muttered.
"Yes, I could have, but my way is more appropriate," I said and sheathed the bloody blade I was holding. The elder of the Witch Council let out a heavy sigh and came down the stairs muttering, "Damn stupid bloodsuckers." "Not all of us are stupid," I said cheerfully and smirked. Davina halted before Tristan and eyed him nervously.
"Are you going to bite me?" she asked and glared at the back of his head.
"If I wanted to bite you," he said, not turning around. "I would've done it sooner."
"Fair enough," she huffed. "Are you going to give me back my magic you stole from me or not?"
"Mmm," he said thoughtfully and turned to face her. "What will you trade for it?"
"In truth, I shouldn't give you anything for it since it was you who took my magic in the first place."
"Will an apology do?" he drawled.
"Fuck you." He sighed, and then Davina let out a squeak as he grabbed her and forced her eyes to his. She let out a scream as Adaira and I were thrown across the room. My head smacked against the wall, and I cursed as stars danced in my vision. After what seemed like forever, Davina's scream turned into a moan, and the suffocating power of Tristan lifted. Adaira moaned weakly as I cautiously sat up. I looked around to find Davina curled into herself on the floor and clutching her head as she groaned and cursed my sire who was standing over her.
"Forgive me," Tristan said dryly. "I didn't know it was going to hurt."
Davina glared up at him. "You so did know!" she yelled and got slowly to her feet, wincing. "You arrogant fucking moron!" She yanked a blade from one of his many sheathes and gutted him. Snarling, I lunged for her? only to find that I couldn't even move a muscle. Staring furiously at Tristan, I could do nothing but watch, because telling him to release me would accomplish nothing. Hissing as Davina stabbed him a second time, Tristan grabbed her wrist and squeezed until the knife dropped into his other hand. Sheathing the blade, he yanked her to him and sank his fangs into her neck with a snarl. A long second past, before he withdrew and glared darkly at her.
"Don't ever," he growled. "Do that again."
"Let me go," Davina said, grunting as she attempted to break out of his hold. "I'll knee you in the balls if you don't let me go," she warned.
"Then I'll simply have to bite you again," he said and tossed her bodily up the stairs. A pale hand flashed and caught her before she could go through a window.
"Such a pity," Tristan said, sighing.
"Can you let me go now?" I grumbled. The invisible vice-like grip vanished, and I glanced at Adaira who was staring at nothing, half asleep. I pointed to her. "Want to do something about that?"
Tristan glanced at where I was pointing and glared at the witch. "You cut her, you feed her. If I end up touching her, I may end up snapping her neck before I get the chance to talk to her."
"Fine, fine," I grumbled and crawled to the witch. Ripping open my wrist, I pressed it to Adaira's mouth. "Drink," I said, staring deeply into her half-closed eyes. Her expression went blank, and I felt the pull of my blood being drawn and swallowed. I pulled my wrist away and licked it close. "Nap time is over," I said dryly as her eyes widened.
"Is it?" Tristan asked dryly, cursing as he flipped on the light. I winced as his pale skin began to redden slightly.
"Tristan!" Adaira exclaimed and knocked my arm aside as she scrambled to her feet. "You should be dead," she snapped. "How are you up?" I watched as my sire pulled out a pure white blade and held it to the light. The blade shimmered with silver, and Adaira paled. "Where the fuck did you get that?"
"That's the million-dollar question, isn't it?" Tristan asked in a low tone as he sheathed the magical blade.
"Where did you get that?" she hissed.
He shrugged. "If you must know, a witch gave it to us."
"What are you going to do to me?"
"Oh? I don't know," he said thoughtfully. "Sweetheart, what do you think I should do to the witch who fried my brain, hmm?"
"I have no idea," I said chirpily. "Give her an aneurism? Oh, wait, that will kill her." I frowned in thought as Adaira grew paler.
"Hmm," he said thoughtfully. "A little birdie once told me, if a witch is stabbed with a lithium blade, it knocks a witch out for three days and zaps him or her of magic." He smirked. "But your magic will return in half an hour after waking." My skin crawled as his energy filled the room. "We can't have that now," he said softly, and in the blink of an eye, he stabbed Adaira in the leg. "Can we?" he finished as the witch screamed. This time however, she didn't slip into unconsciousness. Adaira kicked out with her other leg as Tristan closed in on her. He caught it before she could connect with his own. She pummeled him with her fists as he leaned down, his hand on the hilt of the blade. She turned green as the blade was pushed deeper. He released it and cupped her chin as her hand flew to the hilt of the blade. Tears and sweat poured down her cheeks as she vainly tried to pull it out. Tristan's smile was creepy as he stared deeply into her dark brown eyes. "That blade, sweetheart, is not going anywhere. So don't bother with trying to remove it." He sighed. "I also can't have you bleeding out on me, either," he growled in annoyance. Baring his fangs, he ripped opened his wrist and pressed it to her mouth. His hold on her chin tightened as she tried to turn her head away from the blood. "None of that now," he chided, her expression going blank. "Drink," he said, almost gently, and I shivered.
"Ow," I said, wincing as the wound closed over the lithium blade. "Ow," I said again and got to my feet. "Do I get to watch?" Tristan released Adaira and stepped back from her. She moaned and sobbed in pain, her leg twitching and jerking. Every time it did that, the witch turned green.
"A quick death for you wouldn't do, sweet Adaira," Tristan said in a deadly tone. "If I had to suffer a week of agonizing pain, then you shall as well. It's only fitting, don't you think?"
"Go to hell!" Adaira screamed, and then groaned.
"I'm already there," he said softly, and then the red vanished from his eyes, leaving them solid white, and filled with rage. Seeing this, the witch froze, her screams of pain turning into short burst of gasps and whimpers. Tristan reached down and plucked her off the floor, and the witch let out a bloodcurdling scream at the sudden move. He hugged her struggling body to him, and the evil smile she couldn't see was chilling. With a finger, he tilted Adaira's head back until she was looking him in the eye. "The pain in your leg," he growled. "Is nothing to what's to come." I suddenly couldn't breathe, as the air thrummed with barely leashed power. "But first," Tristan whispered in her ear. "Let me give you a taste of what you, my dear, have put me through." He smirked. "I'm still suffering from the aftermath of almost having my brain melted."
"No," Adaira moaned. Tristan's eyes narrowed on her, and I shivered at the low growl emanating from him. He released the witch, and she dropped heavily to the floor with a scream. That scream grew louder and more shrilled as she began to writhe. Blood began to pour from her eyes, and Tristan barely got out of the way before she vomited. When she threw up blood a few seconds later, he let out an irritated growl. Adaira finally passed out, and the silence was bliss to my throbbing ears.
"That," I said dryly to the unconscious witch. "Was just a taste of what he went through. If he had given you the full blast of it, your brain wouldn't stand a chance under the onslaught." I walked over to Tristan as Evelyn appeared in the room.
"Take a breather," she said to Tristan before disappearing with the witch. He glared at where she was standing a split second ago and put a hand on my shoulder. With a sigh, he teleported.
A second later, I found myself standing in the living room of his residential home. Pulling away from Tristan, I walked into the kitchen and straight for the box of chocolate chip cookies on the table. Before I could even reach for it, the cookies disappeared. "Oh, come on!" I exclaimed. "Just one, please?"
"How about you jump in the shower," Tristan said from behind me. Grumbling under my breath, I turned and left the kitchen.

Chapter Twenty-five

AISLEY

"The head of the Vampiric Council is dead!" Shae shouted to the whole pride gathered in the auditorium of an abandon theater just outside San Diego. Cheers, hollers and excited hoots filled the small space as she stood at center stage, smirking, a gleam to her dark blue cat-like eyes. Getting to my feet along with them, I whooped and cheered, but inside, I was disgusted. Couldn't we all just get along and none of this, who-has-the-bigger-dick shit? Shae's obsession with wiping out the vampire race was just laughable. Yes, she took down a Council Member about a year ago, but something was telling me that it was pure luck on her part. No one kills a Tronis and live long enough to tell the tale a year later. Hell, not even a day. Shae living this long was again, pure luck, and oh, let's not forget the witches. Why, why, why was I even born into this god forsaken Pride? Each pride was a huge ass happy family. But over the centuries, outsiders were brought in, and they were considered as extended family. The walls on either side of me had stains of something I didn't even want to ponder on. There were holes and cracks here and there. Chapter Twenty-six

KIRA

Oh, I said silently to myself, pressing my fingers into my temples and letting out a long sigh. Why, oh why were the shifters here? One of the witches barely jumped away in time, as a lightning bolt struck where she stood a split second ago.

She shook her head. "We're too busy trying to keep the shields up," she said, grunting with the effort.

Jailyn closed her eyes, shuddering. I looked up as Evelyn jumped from the roof, landing in a mess of gore. She looked around, and I took a step back as rage came over her. Growling, I jerked my fangs out and tossed the drained body at another one. Before I could so much as think about getting up, someone grabbed me and bashed my head into the side of the building. "For all of our sakes, don't bring Jordana up."

"Sire," Jordana said blankly and again blinked. "I'm bored." She frowned. "You're covered in blood." She poked a finger into my stomach, and I grunted. "What happened? Did you kill someone?"

"There was an earthquake? so to speak."

"It's bad, I'll tell you that now." She grunted. "Just don't puke, okay? There's already enough blood seeping into the earth." Jordana drained her bag of blood and crushed the plastic in her hand as a ding sounded. We stepped off the elevator and pushed our way outside.
The smell of blood, smoke, fear, rage, the wounded, and the dead were like a punch to the gut. Talk about sensory overload, I thought and waved Jailyn over. The necromancer appeared before us, and she whispered something to Jordana. A second later, my childe was off running, and I let out a groan, because I knew exactly what she was going to do. Jailyn smirked. "Is there a problem, hunter?" she asked, and then she laughed as I glared at her. She put a hand on my head, and I shuddered as the lingering effect of death magic wrapped around me. "What do you need?"
"Anyone else we know left us?"
"Yes, Byron and?" She frowned in thought. "Preston."
I nodded. "Did Isabelle uh?"
"Did she ask me to bring her sister back? Yes, she did."
"I'm guessing you didn't grant her wish?"
The necromancer sighed and stared off into the distance. She dropped her hand from me and leaned against the wall beside the opened doorway. She pulled me to her other side as more hunters stepped from the building to help with the massive cleanup. "I'm going to ask you something that you will not like." I stiffened. "I want you to think about it for a minute, and I want an honest answer."
I gulped and took in a deep breath of polluted air. "Ask it."
Her unblinking gaze met mine, and I froze as she held me ensnared. And it wasn't compulsion she was using. The feeling of bone-numbing cold settled over me as she placed her pale hands on either side of my head. "Remember," she said, both out loud and into my mind. "I want you to think about it, not react. Think." I nodded mutely. "If you were to lose Sven today, you would want me to bring him back, yes?" I nodded. "What if he doesn't want to be brought back? Will you let him be?"
"If he wishes not to come back to the living, then I'll let him be," I said softly. "No matter of what I think."
Jailyn nodded. "Isabelle wants her sister back, but Tory doesn't wish to return to the living." I nodded. "What I am saying is this. As much as I would like to bring everyone back from the dead, and just as I respect the wishes of the living-I also have to respect the wishes of the dead just the same."
I shuddered and nodded. "I understand."
She nodded, taking a step back from me. "I just wanted you to understand."
I rubbed my arms, shivering. "I do." She grunted, before disappearing in a swirl of smoke and the stink of sulfur.

Chapter Thirty-four

LORENA

Sighing, and shaking off the clinging effect of magic on my skin, I scanned the battle scene around me in thought. Catching sight of hunters trying to subdue Tristan, I walked over to them. "Can I help?" I asked, holding back a smile as a hunter let out a vicious curse.

TRISTAN

"That is your fifth human," Jailyn said from far, far away. With a mental snarl, I withdrew my fangs and shoved the human away from me. Jailyn's cold hand rested on my upper arm and squeezed gently. "Are you all right?" she asked softly. If I could see anything but red, then perhaps, but it was useless as I tried to blink the red haze away without any success. The loud roar in my ears was my constant companion as I struggled to come back to my senses.
