During the long battle, I felt three deaths? well, more than three. Vampires were dying all around the world, but the three particular deaths I felt were more painful, and therefore, bound to get my attention. Not only vampires I've directly sired were painful, but if a vampire died nearby, say a few yards or a mile from me, that death was also attention-grabbing, especially when it felt like your head was being torn from your shoulders. I inwardly groaned. God how I wish I could sleep for eternity, away from this craving I struggled with every second of my existence, away from watching the world change as I remain the same, watching people dying left and right-whether it was from starvation, slavery, sickness, or just plain cruelty. How I wish I could get away from all of that, and so, so much more. I wanted nothing more than to curl up into a ball and wish for death. If someone told you that living forever was a grand idea, he or she must be out of their fucking minds. Because five thousand years of existing was fucking torture. Yes, there were good things in my life that I appreciate and still do, but centuries of fighting with your inner beast could be entertaining for only so long. It was also very, very, very boring when you saw everything and experienced all the world had to offer. And yes, I welcome death, and a lot of people wanted me dead. It was either that, or they wanted my powers for themselves. But I was sure as fucking hell not going to just lie down and present my throat and belly to my enemies. I was not going to go down without a god damn fight. "Earth to Tristan." I blinked, registering that someone was slapping my arm. "You in there?" Jailyn drawled. "Sorry," I muttered.

Luckily no one was in the chamber as I let my forehead hit the table with a thump-my hands smacking the surface. Chapter Thirty-six

VIVIANA

It felt like someone was scraping the inside of my stomach raw with a serrated knife. And that someone? Had no thought of stopping anytime soon. The gnawing pain of hunger was all I could think about as I sat, curled up into a tight ball against the wall of my cell. How long had I been down here? Weeks? Months? Years? Did I even want to know? Did I even care? I let out a moan, and then I froze as I felt someone outside my cell door. I stopped breathing altogether. No one ever came down here unless it was to give each of us a small plastic cup of warm fresh blood every other day, or to lock someone else up. Well, that was usually the case until-has it been a couple of days ago-when a few vampires came down here for some reason. We were told to keep silent unless we wanted to die a painful death. None of us made a sound all right. Not even when a horn sounded a few minutes after their arrival. Or like that one time when my heart went into overdrive for no apparent reason as someone did a walkthrough and decided to give me a heart attack by entering my cell. He fed me a cup of his blood which was by the way, heaven within itself. He also up my level of fear a notch when he confirmed he was a Council member. I couldn't remember much about that night. All I remembered was him, the blood, and the feeling of humiliation. I inwardly shuddered and kept my eyes closed, waiting for whatever was to come in the next few seconds. I still didn't move or make a sound as I heard the painful scrape of the door being unlocked and open. "We both know that you're really not asleep," a female voice said dryly. "Get up." I opened my eyes and blinked at the wall. Did she say get up, or was that just my imagination? She sighed, and I mentally shook myself. Groaning, I uncurled from my position onto my hands and knees. Taking a deep breath, I slowly got up and turned to face her. "My name is Liana, and I would like for you to turn around." She glanced behind her as I did as she said. "All of you as well," she continued. "Stand up and face the wall with your hands behind your back," she finished as I felt the cold cuff snapping around my wrist. I stiffened and winced as something bit into my skin. The other cuff snapped around my other wrist, and I felt a hand on my shoulder, turning me around. My skin crawled as I saw more vampires appearing outside my cell. What was going on? I thought as she led me out of my own cell. The door slammed with a resounding boom, and I shivered as the whole situation reminded me of a show called Lock Up. The steel on steel was painful to my ears, and I grimaced as I came to a stop in the middle of an empty room. The only exit I saw were the one leading back to the cells, the elevator, and a closed door that led somewhere. I wanted to ask what was going on, but at the moment, I still valued my life. My inmates joined me, and every one of them was cuffed and had a scary-looking vampire behind them. "Sven, we good to go?" the one behind me asked.
"We are," a male voice replied.
"Are we doing this the short way?"
"No, we're doing this the long way." The hell were they talking about? I thought as what sounded like an intercom beep going off. "We're ready to go," Sven said to whoever was waiting on the other end.
"Good," another female voice replied. "Turn them to face the camera."
"Are you serious?"
"Do it," she warned. "I'm just doing my job here." Sven sighed, but nodded. Liana turned me to face the closed door, and it suddenly felt like a thousand eyes were trained on me. "All accounted for," the female voice said a few seconds later.
"Yes," Sven said dryly. "Tell Tristan to do his thing so we can go up."
"Tell me that yourself," a deep voice growled.
"Oh, hey sire, how's it going?" In answer, a female robotic voice said, "Lockdown initiated for the next twelve hours." There was a loud boom, and the entire building shook slightly.
"If any of you are claustrophobic," Tristan said over the intercom. "I am truly sorry."
"Sorry my ass," Liana muttered before everything went dark. An evil laugh sounded in my head as the air became harder and harder to breathe. I let out a gasp, and when I couldn't hear myself or anything else, I began to struggle. Everything felt numb as I made contact with something or someone. Shit, what the hell was happening to me? The slight pressure in my head I hadn't noticed earlier became more pronounced as I continued struggling to get free of? whatever this was. Relax, Tristan whispered into my mind. Just? relax. He must be out of his ever-loving fucking mind, I mentally yelled. I couldn't see, hear anything but him in my head, and I could barely feel anything. And he wanted me to fucking relax. Yeah, out of his fucking mind. Just as sudden as my vision and hearing went away, it came back to me in a rush. I staggered, and Liana released me, letting me painfully hit the floor in an awkward heap. My other inmates also hit the floor cursing, groaning, moaning, gasping, or all of the above.
"Un-cuff them," another female voice said, and I lifted my head to find her sitting at a table with four others. "And give them some? refreshments. They look? quite hungry."
"How many pints?" one of the vampires near us asked.
"Four pints each shall do," Tristan growled. "We need them to be able to think? shall I say, clearly?" he asked and chuckled. The cuffs around my wrists popped open, and I was able to push myself into a sitting position.
Looking around, I could see that we were in a huge darkened room of some kind, with high ceiling, concrete walls, a table in the center, and in the middle of the floor, I could see a drain. A small bin with a closed lid was put in front of me, and I actually let out a whimper as I picked it up and snapped off the lid. Inside were four clear plastic bags of blood, and from the heat that was wafting from the container, it was nice and hot, if not warm. Salivating, I reached for one of the bags, only to growl in frustration when my hand came to a stop on its own, just inches from touching it. My hungry gaze was jerked from the red liquid, and I found myself staring into pitched black eyes. My vision blurred, and I couldn't turn my head or blink to clear it. "Don't make a mess," she said out loud and into my mind. "For once, drink like civilized vampires." I blinked, and I could've sworn I saw writhing shadows behind her as I settled my gaze back on the blood. Taking the hot bag of blood in hand, I brought it to my mouth and sank my fangs into it, drinking it like it was a juice box when all I wanted to do was rip into the bags and gulp down the blood like there was no tomorrow. Forget about what I think or don't think, living was sounding like a good idea by the second. Yes, living was good? very good. Shaking my head, I finished my second bag and reached for a third.
"Hunters," Tristan said over the sound of crinkling bags. "You may leave if you like." Hunters? I thought, and my eyes widened as Sven, Liana, and another female hunter shook their heads while the rest either pushed the double doors open and filed out, or went behind the heavy black curtains blocking the back portion of the room from us. What did he mean by hunters? "I mean exactly that," he said, and I yelped as he looked directly at me. "Their main job is to hunt rogue vampires." I swallowed my last mouthful of blood and stared at the empty bags, wanting more. "I didn't catch your name when we? first met. Then again, you were not as lucid as you are now."
"Viviana," I mumbled. In my peripheral vision, I saw him nodding. I wanted to ask if I could have more blood, but? I mentally shrugged and set the bin on the floor. Hoping I wasn't going to be drained, kicked, punched, gutted, stabbed, shot, or bitten, I slowly got to my feet. Wait, do vampires eat each other? Oh god, that sounded so wrong, on so many levels. Tristan leaned back in his chair, and laughed. Jailyn looked at him like he'd lost it completely, and then smirked. He leaned in and whispered something in her ear even my heighten hearing couldn't pick up on. And shit, he was reading my mind. Were they all reading my mind? Talk about the lack of privacy, I silently muttered to myself.
"Yes," Tristan said dryly. "We're reading your minds, or rather? I am." He scanned the room and nodded to someone behind me. "I believe they are satisfied? for now." Liana picked up my bin of empty bags, going around and collecting the others as Tristan rose from his chair. He came around the table, hands in his pockets. "Do you know where you all are?" We shook our heads, and he smirked. "Good, if you did, I might just have to kill you where you stand," he said, his voice turning into a growl toward the end, causing my skin to prickle in alarm.
"You're in the chamber of the Council," someone else said before he could continue. I stiffened, and hoped tonight wasn't going to be my last.
He sighed. "Would you like to take over, Evelyn?" someone I presumed to be Evelyn, got up and rounded the table to his side. She gave him a hard look. "What?" he asked, glaring at her.
"Go and sit," she said, glaring right back at him. Her eyes narrowed when he didn't move. She leaned in and whispered something I couldn't hear.
"Such a pity," he growled and slowly went back to his seat.
"I am Evelyn," she said, returning her attention to us. "Though we don't usually give out introductions, I'm going to anyways." She nodded to Tristan. "That is Tristan as some of you already know." She took in a deep breath, letting it out in a heavy sigh. "That is Jailyn, Elijah, and Taylor," she continued, nodding to each one of them. "If you all survive this night, you can do what you all do best, which is of course, gossiping away about how insane and evil the Council members are."
"That is such an understatement of the century if I ever heard one," Jailyn muttered.
"Evelyn," Tristan growled. "Let's not feed them possible ideas just yet. Let's skip the nicety and get to it. Shall we?"

SATHIA

The purple surrounding of the abyss was? let's just say, why did it have to be purple? Why can't it be red? Or Green? How about just plain old grey for fuck sake? The abyss was a carbon copy of the living world. The only difference was the fact that the buildings here were all a crumbling pile of ruins, and this realm was inhabited by spirits-mostly confused spirits who wandered aimlessly with nowhere to go, and no sense of directions. And some spirits stuck around for whatever reason. Anyone with the ability to jump plane could come and go as they like. Usually people with this ability, were necromancers, and a powerful one at that. This was the in between, not hell. Because if it was hell, you had to fight to stay alive. Not that the abyss was any different. Here, you had to run away from hungry spirits. Here, time either moved slow, or fast, or the same. Hell, this place had a mind of its own. And the only way to tell time was if you were attuned with it. Like the vampires and their internal clockwork thing they had going on. Shaking my head, I dug a talon into the black pillar beside me and let out a hiss of annoyance. Waiting for Xorik was like waiting for a child stuck neck deep in displays of colorful wrappers and different smells of a shop filled with everything candy. Why Jailyn liked him, I had no idea. The necromancer he was tracking for the past months was doing a mighty fucking job staying off the radar. What was it that he had in motion? To go through all lengths in keeping himself off the grid told me that he had something planned, and something big. The skittering of pebbles on black asphalt sounded off to my right, and I turned as a tiny creature scuttled toward me and stopped just out of reach. Xorik huffed out a breath, and red sparks flew from his mouth, briefly showering the area with tiny dancing flames. "What did you find?" I hissed and spat acid on the ground where it sizzled briefly before eating through it.
"I think I'm on to him," Xorik lisped, his tail whipping through the air in agitation.
"You said that countless times before," I growled. "What has changed?"
"I was eavesdropping on a group of necromancers."
I stiffened. "And?"
The red glow in his eyes seemed to glow brighter as he gave an evil grin. "They said something about drowning the world in blood and fire."
"Nothing new there," I hissed. "The vampires and shifters have been doing that for thousands of years and counting."
He shrugged. "That may be true. But in this one, all the humans along with vampires, shifters, and witches will die if this necromancer gets his way." I smirked as I mentally did a high-five with the devil. We demons love blood, chaos and destruction, and I wasn't any different. The more blood spilled? The better. Then I let out a sigh. I was fine being bound to Jailyn, but being controlled by a group of power-hungry necromancers was not in my book, especially when I didn't know shit about them to begin with. I knew Jailyn before she became a vampire, and that was four thousand years longer than these fuckers. "Shall I continue my? spying?" He looked around the desolate place nervously, tail curling about himself.
"Is Jailyn summoning you?" I asked.
"No, no. Just making sure she's not here."
I smirked. "You don't want to tell her what you've told me a few seconds ago. Is that it?"
He snorted. "Fine, you tell her, and see if she sets you on fire."
"She did not set you on fire," I said dryly.
"How would you know?" he asked. "You weren't there. I may be a demon who breathes fire, but it still hurts when you're the center of the flame's focus." I shook my head as he spread his wings and launched himself into the air.
"We're not that easy to kill you know."
"You want to test out that theory? She was going to stab me with that glowing blade. And you know if that thing goes through my heart, I am toast. I think I prefer decapitation," he muttered, and then let out a screech, almost falling as Jailyn appeared between us. I couldn't help it; I smiled as he righted himself and stared guiltily at her. "Mistress," he said cheerfully. "It is so good to see you."
Jailyn inclined her head and looked at him curiously. "Did you forget to tell me something before I'd sent you away?" she asked suspiciously.
"I didn't forget to tell you anything. What makes you think such?"
She put up a finger and frowned. "One, you addressed me as mistress, and you only do that when you've done something wrong, or think I'm going to not like what you have to tell me." She put up another finger. "And two, you are as nervous as a skittish rabbit." She dropped her hand, shaking her head. "So," she said with a heavy sigh. "Are you going to tell me?"

Her lips twitched. "No, it is not over yet. There's a thirty-minute break." He let out a squeak as she snatched him from the air. "And don't you change the subject on me," she warned. "Tell me little demon, or I swear I will drop you in a pentagram and hold you prisoner for a century. How long do you think you'll last before you go insane? Hmm?"
"No circle," Xorik hissed. "No square, no tri-okay okay," he squeaked as Jailyn growled low in her throat. As he continued, telling her what he told me, the red in Jailyn's eyes slowly faded.
"They didn't say anything else?" she asked softly.
Xorik shook his head. "They went back to reading and muttering and? normal stuff." He blinked, as if remembering something. "There were witches with them."
"What?" Jailyn and I growled.
Jailyn stared off into the distance, her eyes unfocused. "This just gets better and better. Doesn't it?" she growled to herself. Sighing, she set Xorik on the ground. "I want you to find out more about what they're trying to do." Xorik nodded as she turned to look at me. "And Sathia, I would like you to join him."
I grunted. "Of course."
"If you find yourself in danger, call me. Is that understood?"
"Yes," Xorik and I said in unison. Nodding and giving us one last hard look, she disappeared in a swirl of frigid air.

Apparently the necklace around my neck worked, because I felt no stinging pain as the light came on. "Well, damn," Brynna grumbled. "I was hoping that it didn't work so I could kill the fucking witch." She sighed dramatically. "I don't get to have fun anymore."
"Stop bitching," Sven grumbled, and then cursed as the scent of blood filled the air. "You're fucking insane," he hissed. I slowly turned from the window and glared at them both.
"Put," I growled. "That. Blade. Away. Now." With a sigh, she sheathed the blade she was holding.
"Did you call us here for something, sire?"
"Walk with me," I said and teleported, taking them with me.
Outside the Council building, I looked up toward the sky and inwardly groaned. Mentally shaking myself, I took the steps up to the parking lot and started walking in a random direction. "Did you pick a fledgling?" I finally asked as they kept pace with me.
"Yes," Sven said as Brynna nodded.
"What about the rest of the hunters, do they have their fledglings?"
Brynna nodded. "I made sure each hunter had a fledgling."
"Good. Now, are you both all right with leading this?" I scowled, searching for the correct word.
"Training?" Sven offered. "Mentorship?" I grunted. "I'm all for leading them."
"Same," said Brynna.
"Good, I don't have to assign someone else," I said, stopping on the corner of Ashton and Jefferson Avenue. I leaned casually against the signpost and discreetly looked around. Cars past by on the streets, but no one else was near. "I am putting Ari with you two. I didn't address this when the Council was in session, but Evelyn and Jailyn thought it would be a great idea to have them be spies."
"You mean spying on the rogues?" Brynna asked. "Undercover?"
"Yes. But in order to be a proper spy, they must learn how to defend themselves and kill without thinking twice if need be." They nodded.
"What if not all want to become spies for the Council?" Sven asked.
I smirked. "Oh," I said dryly. "I think they all will."
He chuckled, nodding knowingly. "Ah, I see," he said as I felt a rogue silently closing in on us. She came to an abrupt stop thirty feet off to my left and swallowed.
"You're the Council," she said, loud enough for us to hear. Sven and Brynna shook their heads while I just stood there, giving no indication that I had heard. I could see the hairs on her arms standing on end, and she hadn't fed for days-her hunger punching me in the guts. I was a little surprised to see that she was clean. Her long reddish-brown hair and pale skin were not greasy, no dried blood on the corners of her mouth, chin, neck, under her fingernails, or in her hair. Her clothes were also clean-freshly washed and not rumpled-looking or stained with weeks old blood. The only way I knew that she was a rogue was her eyes. They were hunger-filled and wild-looking. I could have mistaken her as a civilian, if I didn't know better. Interesting, I thought as I slipped into her mind. Of course, the first thing I saw was blood. "Hunters then?"
"Who is asking? Sven asked, not looking at her. Brynna casually slipped her hand into her pocket, and I knew it was wrapped around the hilt of a blade.
"Calista."
"What can we do for you, Calista?"
"Kill me." Both Sven and Brynna blinked at that, and I smiled as I slipped from her head. She had forgone feeding until she couldn't stand it any longer. Then she would kill mercilessly-having no sense of herself whatsoever.
"I'm sorry, but what did you say?"
Rubbing her arm, she walked over to us, stopping beside me. "Kill me," she repeated. A split second later, a blade was flipping end-over-end. It struck her in the chest and into her heart.
"My pleasure," Brynna said as I growled low in my throat. Gurgling, Calista wrapped her hand around the hilt and yanked it out with a pained gasp. Jaw clenched, I took the blade from her. Brynna snatched her weapon back as I took the rogue into my arms and pressed my mouth to her jugular.
"Tell me something," I growled. "Why do you want them to kill you?"
"Do you need a reason?" she wheezed. "I'm a rogue."
I pulled back and chuckled. "No, we don't," I said and narrowed my eyes on her. "No rogue ever asked to be killed. I was just curious is all." My brain demanding that I drained her, I inhaled deeply and inwardly groaned as I shoved the rogue toward Sven. He dragged the rogue away from me and the streets, disappearing into the shadows. "Take care of them," I said to Brynna, nodding to the few humans that were getting out of their cars. Grumbling under her breath, she walked over to them, reassuring them that everything was under control and that no one was dead. The last part wasn't true of course, but they didn't need to know that. If I had to deal with freaked out humans at the moment, I'd more likely kill them than comfort them. One of the humans ran past Brynna, and I shook my head as she tried to stop the blonde.
"She was a rogue, wasn't she?" the human asked, stopping in front of me.
My eyes narrowed. "Excuse me?"
"The one that got stabbed in the chest, she's a rogue vampire, right?"
"Who are you?"
She cleared her throat and shifted nervously. "Sorry," she said, glancing at the ground. "Sorry, I'm Tabitha, Tabitha Henlie."
"Ah," I said, trying very hard not to lunge for her pretty neck. "Do you perhaps have a daughter name Skyler?"
"Yes, Skyler is my daughter." She looked up at me. "How is she? We kept in contact, but I haven't seen her since?"
"You don't need to continue," I said, holding out my hand to her. "It is a pleasure to meet you, I am Tristan." Tabitha took my cold hand into her warm one and shook. The warmth from her hand practically seeped into my skin, and I gritted my teeth. It was all I could do not to pull her close and sink my fangs into the side of her neck. For one, Skyler would kick my ass, and two, I didn't want her to run away screaming afterwards. Sven and Brynna joined us, and Sven came to stand close to my side, hand on my shoulder.
"Pleasure to meet you, too," Tabitha said as I slowly withdrew my hand from hers.
"Skyler is doing very well."
She nodded. "Good. That is good," she said and then frowned. "She's not in danger, is she? She wouldn't tell me anything when we talk over the phone or through email."
"She is fine," I said, inwardly wincing. "She has a very, very good sire who will do anything and everything to keep her from harm."
"Okay, but-"
"Mrs. Henlie, look at me." Tabitha looked into my eyes, and smiling, I let my compulsion wash over her. "It was nice meeting you, Tabitha. Your daughter is doing very well, and as much as I love for you to stick around, you must go. Get back into your car and go home. I will be sure to have Skyler give you a call." I reached out and gently turned her away from me. "Go now, and may we meet again, soon." Releasing her, I watched as she walked back to her car, got in, and drove off. After a long moment of silence, Sven removed his hand from my shoulder and stepped in front of me.
"I took care of her," he said and glared at Brynna. "Next time, don't stab someone out in public."
Brynna snorted. "Like you haven't before." I put up a hand, shutting them both up.
"Sven, how is Jordana?"
A pained look cross his eyes before it was gone. "She is better," he said grimly. "In better, I mean she's no longer curled up in a corner, beating herself." He grimaced. "Oh, you know what I mean." He sighed, rubbing his temple. "I can't believe she stopped herself from killing the baby. For a moment there, I thought she was going to lose it. I'm just glad she was able to take out her anger on the two rogues."
"Indeed," I said, nodding. "And what of Hannah Sulli?"
"I have a few hunters patrolling her neighborhood. I've also informed Trynnadon to keep a lookout as well."
"Very good. Now then, shall we head back? According to Jailyn, Skyler made us dinner."
"I heard about that," Brynna said as I stepped away from the post and started walking.
Back at Council HQ, we hit the elevator down to the compound. The moment we reached it, the smell of food hit us. Shaking my head, wondering how in the world it came to this, we stepped out, and I raised my hand to cover my eyes from the bright glare of the lights. We followed the sound of voices to the central part of the entire compound. Dropping my hand, I looked to find a bunch of vampires sitting or standing around a table full of food and drinks. "If I leave now, do you think they will forgive me?" I said to Brynna, low enough for only her to hear. In answer, she pointed to Ari who was looking right at me. "Damn," I muttered.
"Nice try," she said, laughing as she went to join Vaelin, Lorena, and Violet. Letting out a long, long suffering sigh, I went over to Ari, Sven, Liana, and Jordana. I dropped down on the couch beside Jordana, who was picking at her steak and staring unseeingly in front of her.
"Here," Ari said, handing a plate to me. I glanced at the contents, and my mouth watered even more at the sight of blood. "I told Skyler to cook yours extra rare." Setting the plate on my lap, I picked up my knife and fork and grudgingly began to eat? or tried to as my fangs continued to pop out. I sighed as Ari laughed. Forcing my fangs to stay sheathed for more than five seconds, I methodically ate. The sound of voices, silverwares hitting plates, ice clinking against glasses, I blocked them all out as I concentrated on keeping myself in the right frame of mind. After a few more bites, I set my plate on the table in front of me and turned to Jordana who was still picking at her food. I took the fork from her hand and stabbed a bite size piece of steak and prodded her mouth with it.
"Open," I growled. Her mouth opened slightly, and I forced the food in. "Chew it." Glaring at me, she slowly chewed the food, probably not really tasting what she was eating. Liana took the plate away as I dropped the fork onto it.
"This is so not going to work," she said, smirking.
"I've already gathered that much," I said dryly and got up. Jordana's eyes snapped to focus, she jumped up, grabbing me a split second before I teleported.
In my residential home, I led Jordana to the couch and sat her down. She still didn't say anything as I entered my kitchen and for the refrigerator. Opening it, I grabbed a couple of blood bags and reentered my living room. Sitting down beside Jordana, I handed one to her. For once she didn't complain as she ripped into the bag, growling as I punctured my own. As I sipped at the cold contents of the bag, I stared up at the ceiling, wondering what tomorrow would bring, wondering if Jordana would ever be sane again, wondering if the world would ever be the same. Because according to Evelyn's vision, it was more likely that we would all be dead when it was all said and done.


* * * * * *



Epilogue Four Months Later

JAILYN

Alone in my office for the time being, I stared at my computer screen, scowling. I had no idea what I was reading or what I was supposed to do. This is so not my thing, I thought as I put the computer to sleep. Before I could even think about getting up, my office door burst open, and Sathia-in human form-flew in, gasping. Highly alarmed by this, I watched as she hit the carpeted floor on her knees in front of me. "Mistress," she hissed. "Please forgive me, but I came as soon as I could get away."
"Sathia," I said. "What is it?"
She bowed her head. "I found out what the necromancers are doing. But it was too late."
I stiffened. "What?" I asked tightly.
"The gate to hell is open," she whispered. A high-pitched ringing started up in my ears, my vision turned red, souls wailed in my head, and a snarl ripped from me as I grabbed my demon and slammed her against the wall. The light overhead sizzled and popped as it went out. "I'm sorry, mistress."
"Why did you not come sooner?" I growled as something heavy crashed to the floor and shattered.
"I didn't know until a few minutes ago." She shuddered and winced as a soul slammed into her. "I came as soon as I saw demons going through." Fuck. My. Life, I mentally snarled and propelled myself from her. Rage in which I hadn't felt in many years washed over me like a suffocating tide as I heard screams outside. It was too late indeed, as I walked to my window and looked outside. On the streets below, people were running in all directions, screaming, crying, in shocked, but all and all, confused and afraid. This was hell on earth, literally. I turned back to Sathia.
"I want you and your friends out there now. Protect as many humans as you can."
"Yes, mistress," she said and slammed headfirst into my window, shattering it as she flew out and shifting into her demon form midair. Breathing heavily, I dropped onto the small desk beside the window, wondering how in the world's fuck this happened. Year after year, it seemed like the world was getting more fucked by the minute. If nothing was done to seal the gate, then everything and everyone was headed down a long, long, long road to disaster, and that road wasn't going to be easy, or pain free.
